A few more notes about Amazon's description of this product: 1. They specify 3 speed settings and 3 heat settings, but this isn't true. There are 3 settings... Period. Low, High, and cool. Low is slow blower with heat. High is fast blower with heat. Cool is fast blower with no heat (and if you want to use low heat, followed by a \\"cool shot\\", you have to cycle through a high power blast of heat first). 2. I really don't know what the purpose is of the \\"ionic\\" feature. For some reason, it's an option, with an associated button and LED that you have to push each time if you want to use it. Sounds like marketing hype if you ask me.

I wanted something that would eliminate me sweating right after the shower while I fix my hair.<br /><br />This is how I use the revlon hot air brush. I towel dry my hair, put my product in, blow dry my hair with a regular blow dryer for 2-3 minutes concentrating the air flow at the back middle of my head at the roots where the thickest part of my hair is using my fingers to lift my hair away from my scalp. Then I section off my hair with the bottom part of hair left out as the first section. I fireup the Revlon hot air brush on high for about 10 seconds, let it get warmed up. I pick up a part of the section of my hair and apply the brush at the scalp and run the brush under the hair and then on top of the hair about 3-5 times on both sides of the hair until dry and then I turn it down to low, and run it down my hair underneath down to the ends, roll the hair up the brush let it sit for 5 seconds, then turn the brush on cool for 5-10 seconds and run the brush down to the ends turning under as I do so. If you aren't careful you will scorch your hair do to the metal on the brush heating up. I don't have any problems of my hair blowing around everywhere like others were saying. This product is what it is, whether it lasts 6 months or 2 years.   313. How it works: 3 settings: High, Low and Cool (the high and low are warm air and the cool blows out the same amount of air as the high setting, but it's cool air, not warm). 3 attachments: small brush, large brush and hard plastic &#34;tube&#34; (focus attachment). Use the High with the focus attachment to dry your hair. Use the low with the small brush for making curls (use when hair is damp, not wet). Use the low with the large brush for styling, volumizing, larger curls or waves or for straightening. I don't know when you would ever use the cool setting, but I suppose some people might find a use for it!<br /><br />I would definitely recommend this as an &#34;at-home&#34; styler or as a &#34;travel&#34; styler and dryer. I wouldn't use it as a dryer unless you didn't have a normal hair dryer. Even though air comes out faster on the high speed than on the low speed, it doesn't blow your hair as well as a real hair dryer. BUT it would definitely be a life saver if you were on vacation and had a hotel with no hair dryer in the room.<br /><br />Things I like about it: Easy to attach and unattach the attachments. Cord swivels as you turn the main part. 2 speeds, Doesn't tangle your hair. The Low setting doesn't blow your hair every which way while you are setting it. The temperature is perfect. Not too hot, but just warm enough. Doesn't overheat your hair like a curling iron can.<br /><br />I had an earlier model of this one, but I melted the bristles when I accidentally plugged it in to my power adapter in Germany, instead of my power converter. So if you travel out of the country, don't use a power adapter. An adapter just changes the plug so you can use their plugs. You would need a power converter which steps down the power from 220 to 110. (I take one converter and 2 or 3 adapters when I travel), plus 2 of those plugs that turn one plug into 3 - off subject, I know. Sorry.

I found myself covering that part as I was styling my hair, but it can also be easily avoided too. Otherwise, this should work great if you don't cover the air suction with your hand and it should never over-heat. Plus, it takes a long time to blow dry with a round brush, and it doesn't seem worth it when the results aren't that great. I've tried curling irons, curling brushes, even flat irons (which totally scorched the ends of my hair). I decided to try this tool because it was inexpensive and I thought what the heck. I LOVE IT. I have had it for a week and every day has been a GREAT hair day. Here is the technique that I use- after shampooing, I use a leave in Garnier product for smoothing split ends, then I blow dry with a regular vented brush (not a round brush) until my hair is just damp. Then I section my hair (top, middle, bottom). I start at the bottom and use the Revlon tool to flip the bottom up. When that part is dry, I let the middle section down and direction that area towards the back and bottom of my head. Finally, I direct the top section back. I smooth through the style with my fingers and use a mist of hairspray- it stays wavy, bouncy, the ends of my hair look smooth, and it holds the style ALL DAY LONG. The whole process including blow drying and then using the Revlon tool once hair is just damp is about 20 minutes, as my hair is shoulder length. I have had no issues with this over heating. I use it on the low heat setting and it gets plenty hot to style my stubborn hair. Love it!!
